    "newString": "    // Handle edge cases\n    if target == 0 {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Target is 0, returning empty subset\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(Vec::new()), 0);\n    }",
    "originalFile": "//! Incremental pruning algorithm for the subset sum problem.\n//!\n//! This algorithm builds subsets level-by-level, starting from pairs (doublets)\n//! and extending by one element at a time. It prunes subsets that exceed the\n//! target sum, exploiting the anti-monotone property: if sum(S) > target,\n//! then sum(S') > target for all supersets S' ⊇ S.\n//!\n//! This is similar to the Apriori algorithm from frequent itemset mining.\n\nuse crate::{verbose_log, AlgorithmResult};\nuse std::collections::HashSet;\n\n/// Represents a subset as a bitmask and its sum.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)]\nstruct SubsetState {\n    /// Bitmask representing which elements are included\n    mask: u64,\n    /// Precomputed sum of the subset\n    sum: u64,\n}\n\nimpl SubsetState {\n    fn new(mask: u64, sum: u64) -> Self {\n        Self { mask, sum }\n    }\n\n    /// Check if element at index i is in this subset\n    fn contains(&self, i: usize) -> bool {\n        (self.mask & (1u64 << i)) != 0\n    }\n\n    /// Create a new subset by adding element at index i with value v\n    fn extend(&self, i: usize, v: u64) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            mask: self.mask | (1u64 << i),\n            sum: self.sum.saturating_add(v),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Incremental pruning subset sum algorithm.\n///\n/// Builds subsets incrementally from pairs (doublets), extending each valid\n/// subset by one element at a time. Prunes subsets that exceed the target,\n/// preventing exploration of all their supersets.\n///\n/// # Algorithm\n///\n/// 1. Check for single-element solutions (k=1)\n/// 2. Generate all pairs (k=2) with sum ≤ target\n/// 3. For each level k, extend valid subsets by adding one unused element\n/// 4. Prune subsets where sum > target (anti-monotone property)\n/// 5. Return when solution found or no valid subsets remain\n///\n/// # Arguments\n///\n/// * `numbers` - Slice of natural numbers to search through\n/// * `target` - Target sum to find\n/// * `verbose` - Enable verbose logging output\n///\n/// # Returns\n///\n/// `AlgorithmResult` containing the solution (if found) and step count\n///\n/// # Time Complexity\n///\n/// O(2^n) worst case, but with early pruning based on sum exceeding target.\n/// Effective when many subsets exceed the target early.\n///\n/// # Space Complexity\n///\n/// O(C(n,k)) where k is the current level - stores all valid subsets at each level.\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// ```\n/// use subset_sum::incremental_pruning;\n///\n/// let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n/// let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 15, false);\n/// assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n/// ```\n#[must_use]\npub fn incremental_pruning(numbers: &[u64], target: u64, verbose: bool) -> AlgorithmResult {\n    let n = numbers.len();\n    let mut steps: u64 = 0;\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Incremental Pruning] Starting with {} numbers, target={}\",\n        n,\n        target\n    );\n    verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] Numbers: {:?}\", numbers);\n\n    // Handle edge cases\n    if target == 0 {\n        verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] Target is 0, returning empty subset\");\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(Vec::new()), 0);\n    }\n\n    if n == 0 {\n        verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] No numbers provided\");\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Limit to 63 bits for bitmask representation\n    if n > 63 {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Too many numbers ({}), falling back to first 63\",\n            n\n        );\n    }\n    let n = n.min(63);\n\n    // Check for single-element solutions (k=1)\n    verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] Checking single elements (k=1)\");\n    for (i, &num) in numbers.iter().take(n).enumerate() {\n        steps += 1;\n        if num == target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Incremental Pruning] Found single element solution: {}\",\n                num\n            );\n            return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(vec![num]), steps);\n        }\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Element {} = {} (not equal to target)\",\n            i,\n            num\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Generate initial pairs (k=2) - the \"doublets\"\n    verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] Generating pairs (k=2)\");\n    let mut current_level: HashSet<SubsetState> = HashSet::new();\n\n    for i in 0..n {\n        for j in (i + 1)..n {\n            steps += 1;\n            let sum = numbers[i].saturating_add(numbers[j]);\n            let mask = (1u64 << i) | (1u64 << j);\n\n            if sum == target {\n                verbose_log!(\n                    verbose,\n                    \"[Incremental Pruning] Found pair solution: {} + {} = {}\",\n                    numbers[i],\n                    numbers[j],\n                    target\n                );\n                return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(vec![numbers[i], numbers[j]]), steps);\n            }\n\n            if sum < target {\n                let state = SubsetState::new(mask, sum);\n                current_level.insert(state);\n                verbose_log!(\n                    verbose,\n                    \"[Incremental Pruning] Valid pair: {} + {} = {} (keeping)\",\n                    numbers[i],\n                    numbers[j],\n                    sum\n                );\n            } else {\n                verbose_log!(\n                    verbose,\n                    \"[Incremental Pruning] Pair {} + {} = {} exceeds target (pruning)\",\n                    numbers[i],\n                    numbers[j],\n                    sum\n                );\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Incremental Pruning] After k=2: {} valid subsets\",\n        current_level.len()\n    );\n\n    // Extend level by level (k=3, 4, 5, ...)\n    let mut k = 2usize;\n    while !current_level.is_empty() && k < n {\n        k += 1;\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Extending to k={}, starting with {} subsets\",\n            k,\n            current_level.len()\n        );\n\n        let mut next_level: HashSet<SubsetState> = HashSet::new();\n\n        for state in &current_level {\n            // Try adding each element not already in the subset\n            for i in 0..n {\n                if state.contains(i) {\n                    continue;\n                }\n\n                steps += 1;\n                let new_state = state.extend(i, numbers[i]);\n\n                if new_state.sum == target {\n                    // Found solution! Reconstruct the subset\n                    let solution: Vec<u64> = (0..n)\n                        .filter(|&j| new_state.contains(j))\n                        .map(|j| numbers[j])\n                        .collect();\n                    verbose_log!(\n                        verbose,\n                        \"[Incremental Pruning] Found solution at k={}: {:?}\",\n                        k,\n                        solution\n                    );\n                    return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(solution), steps);\n                }\n\n                if new_state.sum < target {\n                    // Only keep subsets that don't exceed target\n                    next_level.insert(new_state);\n                }\n                // If sum > target, this subset and all its supersets are pruned\n            }\n        }\n\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] After k={}: {} valid subsets\",\n            k,\n            next_level.len()\n        );\n\n        current_level = next_level;\n    }\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Incremental Pruning] No solution found after {} steps\",\n        steps\n    );\n    AlgorithmResult::new(None, steps)\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_simple_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 15, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        let solution = result.solution.unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(solution.iter().sum::<u64>(), 15);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_no_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![2, 4, 6, 8];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 1, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_none());\n assert!(result.solution.unwrap().is_empty());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_single_element() {\n        let numbers = vec![5];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 5, false);\n result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 10, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        let solution = result.solution.unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(solution.iter().sum::<u64>(), 10);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_pruning_effectiveness() {\n        // Large numbers should get pruned early\n        let numbers = vec![100, 200, 300, 1, 2, 3];\n        let result =     "originalFile": "//! Incremental pruning algorithm for the subset sum problem.\n//!\n//! This algorithm builds subsets level-by-level, starting from pairs (doublets)\n//! and extending by one element at a time. It prunes subsets that exceed the\n//! target sum, exploiting the anti-monotone property: if sum(S) > target,\n//! then sum(S') > target for all supersets S' ⊇ S.\n//!\n//! This is similar to the Apriori algorithm from frequent itemset mining.\n\nuse crate::{verbose_log, AlgorithmResult};\nuse std::collections::HashSet;\n\n/// Represents a subset as a bitmask and its sum.\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Copy, PartialEq, Eq, Hash)]\nstruct SubsetState {\n    /// Bitmask representing which elements are included\n    mask: u64,\n    /// Precomputed sum of the subset\n    sum: u64,\n}\n\nimpl SubsetState {\n    fn new(mask: u64, sum: u64) -> Self {\n        Self { mask, sum }\n    }\n\n    /// Check if element at index i is in this subset\n    fn contains(&self, i: usize) -> bool {\n        (self.mask & (1u64 << i)) != 0\n    }\n\n    /// Create a new subset by adding element at index i with value v\n    fn extend(&self, i: usize, v: u64) -> Self {\n        Self {\n            mask: self.mask | (1u64 << i),\n            sum: self.sum.saturating_add(v),\n        }\n    }\n}\n\n/// Incremental pruning subset sum algorithm.\n///\n/// Builds subsets incrementally from pairs (doublets), extending each valid\n/// subset by one element at a time. Prunes subsets that exceed the target,\n/// preventing exploration of all their supersets.\n///\n/// # Algorithm\n///\n/// 1. Check for single-element solutions (k=1)\n/// 2. Generate all pairs (k=2) with sum ≤ target\n/// 3. For each level k, extend valid subsets by adding one unused element\n/// 4. Prune subsets where sum > target (anti-monotone property)\n/// 5. Return when solution found or no valid subsets remain\n///\n/// # Arguments\n///\n/// * `numbers` - Slice of natural numbers to search through\n/// * `target` - Target sum to find\n/// * `verbose` - Enable verbose logging output\n///\n/// # Returns\n///\n/// `AlgorithmResult` containing the solution (if found) and step count\n///\n/// # Time Complexity\n///\n/// O(2^n) worst case, but with early pruning based on sum exceeding target.\n/// Effective when many subsets exceed the target early.\n///\n/// # Space Complexity\n///\n/// O(C(n,k)) where k is the current level - stores all valid subsets at each level.\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// ```\n/// use subset_sum::incremental_pruning;\n///\n/// let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n/// let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 15, false);\n/// assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n/// ```\n#[must_use]\npub fn incremental_pruning(numbers: &[u64], target: u64, verbose: bool) -> AlgorithmResult {\n    let n = numbers.len();\n    let mut steps: u64 = 0;\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Incremental Pruning] Starting with {} numbers, target={}\",\n        n,\n        target\n    );\n    verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] Numbers: {:?}\", numbers);\n\n    // Handle edge cases\n    if target == 0 {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Target is 0, returning empty subset\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(Vec::new()), 0);\n    }\n\n    if n == 0 {\n        verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] No numbers provided\");\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Limit to 63 bits for bitmask representation\n    if n > 63 {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Too many numbers ({}), falling back to first 63\",\n            n\n        );\n    }\n    let n = n.min(63);\n\n    // Check for single-element solutions (k=1)\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Incremental Pruning] Checking single elements (k=1)\"\n    );\n    for (i, &num) in numbers.iter().take(n).enumerate() {\n        steps += 1;\n        if num == target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Incremental Pruning] Found single element solution: {}\",\n                num\n            );\n            return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(vec![num]), steps);\n        }\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Element {} = {} (not equal to target)\",\n            i,\n            num\n        );\n    }\n\n    // Generate initial pairs (k=2) - the \"doublets\"\n    verbose_log!(verbose, \"[Incremental Pruning] Generating pairs (k=2)\");\n    let mut current_level: HashSet<SubsetState> = HashSet::new();\n\n    for i in 0..n {\n        for j in (i + 1)..n {\n            steps += 1;\n            let sum = numbers[i].saturating_add(numbers[j]);\n            let mask = (1u64 << i) | (1u64 << j);\n\n            if sum == target {\n                verbose_log!(\n                    verbose,\n                    \"[Incremental Pruning] Found pair solution: {} + {} = {}\",\n                    numbers[i],\n                    numbers[j],\n                    target\n                );\n                return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(vec![numbers[i], numbers[j]]), steps);\n            }\n\n            if sum < target {\n                let state = SubsetState::new(mask, sum);\n                current_level.insert(state);\n                verbose_log!(\n                    verbose,\n                    \"[Incremental Pruning] Valid pair: {} + {} = {} (keeping)\",\n                    numbers[i],\n                    numbers[j],\n                    sum\n                );\n            } else {\n                verbose_log!(\n                    verbose,\n                    \"[Incremental Pruning] Pair {} + {} = {} exceeds target (pruning)\",\n                    numbers[i],\n                    numbers[j],\n                    sum\n                );\n            }\n        }\n    }\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Incremental Pruning] After k=2: {} valid subsets\",\n        current_level.len()\n    );\n\n    // Extend level by level (k=3, 4, 5, ...)\n    let mut k = 2usize;\n    while !current_level.is_empty() && k < n {\n        k += 1;\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] Extending to k={}, starting with {} subsets\",\n            k,\n            current_level.len()\n        );\n\n        let mut next_level: HashSet<SubsetState> = HashSet::new();\n\n        for state in &current_level {\n            // Try adding each element not already in the subset\n            for i in 0..n {\n                if state.contains(i) {\n                    continue;\n                }\n\n                steps += 1;\n                let new_state = state.extend(i, numbers[i]);\n\n                if new_state.sum == target {\n                    // Found solution! Reconstruct the subset\n                    let solution: Vec<u64> = (0..n)\n                        .filter(|&j| new_state.contains(j))\n                        .map(|j| numbers[j])\n                        .collect();\n                    verbose_log!(\n                        verbose,\n                        \"[Incremental Pruning] Found solution at k={}: {:?}\",\n                        k,\n                        solution\n                    );\n                    return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(solution), steps);\n                }\n\n                if new_state.sum < target {\n                    // Only keep subsets that don't exceed target\n                    next_level.insert(new_state);\n                }\n                // If sum > target, this subset and all its supersets are pruned\n            }\n        }\n\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Incremental Pruning] After k={}: {} valid subsets\",\n            k,\n            next_level.len()\n        );\n\n        current_level = next_level;\n    }\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Incremental Pruning] No solution found after {} steps\",\n        steps\n    );\n    AlgorithmResult::new(None, steps)\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_simple_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 15, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        let solution = result.solution.unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(solution.iter().sum::<u64>(), 15);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_no_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![2, 4, 6, 8];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 1, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_none());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_target_zero() {\n        let numbers = vec![1, 2, 3];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 0, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        assert!(result.solution.unwrap().is_empty());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_single_element() {\n        let numbers = vec![5];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 5, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        assert_eq!(result.solution.unwrap(), vec![5]);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_pair_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![3, 7, 10];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 10, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        let solution = result.solution.unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(solution.iter().sum::<u64>(), 10);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_pruning_effectiveness() {\n        // Large numbers should get pruned early\n        let numbers = vec![100, 200, 300, 1, 2, 3];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 6, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        assert_eq!(result.solution.unwrap().iter().sum::<u64>(), 6);\n        // Steps should be relatively low due to pruning\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_larger_subset() {\n        let numbers = vec![1, 2, 3, 4, 5];\n        let result = incremental_pruning(&numbers, 12, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        assert_eq!(result.solution.unwrap().iter().sum::<u64>(), 12);\n    }\n}\n",

    "originalFile": "//! Max-first reduction algorithm for the subset sum problem.\n//!\n//! This algorithm works by sorting numbers and recursively trying to include\n//! the largest element first. If including the max doesn't lead to a solution,\n//! it's excluded and the search continues with smaller elements.\n//!\n//! The idea is that by committing to the largest elements early, we can\n//! reduce the target sum faster and potentially prune more of the search space.\n\nuse crate::{verbose_log, AlgorithmResult};\n\n/// Max-first reduction subset sum algorithm.\n///\n/// This algorithm:\n/// 1. Sorts numbers in ascending order\n/// 2. Filters out numbers greater than target\n/// 3. Handles edge cases (target = 0, single element solutions, etc.)\n/// 4. Recursively tries to include the largest element:\n///    - If max <= remaining target: include max, recurse with (target - max)\n///    - If no solution found with max, exclude it and try without\n///\n/// The intuition is that larger numbers reduce the target faster,\n/// potentially leading to earlier termination.\n///\n/// # Arguments\n///\n/// * `numbers` - Slice of natural numbers to search through\n/// * `target` - Target sum to find\n/// * `verbose` - Enable verbose logging output\n///\n/// # Returns\n///\n/// `AlgorithmResult` containing the solution (if found) and step count\n///\n/// # Time Complexity\n///\n/// O(2^n) worst case, but with early pruning when large elements\n/// quickly exceed or reach the target.\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// ```\n/// use subset_sum::max_first_reduction;\n///\n/// let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n/// let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 15, false);\n/// assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n/// ```\n#[must_use]\npub fn max_first_reduction(numbers: &[u64], target: u64, verbose: bool) -> AlgorithmResult {\n    let mut steps: u64 = 0;\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Max-First Reduction] Starting with {} numbers, target={}\",\n        numbers.len(),\n        target\n    );\n\n    // Handle target = 0\n    if target == 0 {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Target is 0, returning empty subset\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(Vec::new()), 0);\n    }\n\n    // Filter numbers: keep only those <= target and > 0\n    let mut sorted: Vec<u64> = numbers\n        .iter()\n        .copied()\n        .filter(|&x| x >= 1 && x <= target)\n        .collect();\n\n    if sorted.is_empty() {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] No valid numbers after filtering\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Sort in ascending order (we'll work from the end for max)\n    sorted.sort_unstable();\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Max-First Reduction] Sorted and filtered numbers: {:?}\",\n        sorted\n    );\n\n    let n = sorted.len();\n    let total_sum: u64 = sorted.iter().sum();\n\n    // Early exit: target impossible\n    if target > total_sum {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Target {} > total sum {}, impossible\",\n            target,\n            total_sum\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Check if total sum equals target (take all)\n    if target == total_sum {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Target equals total sum, returning all numbers\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(sorted), 1);\n    }\n\n    // Check for single element solution\n    if sorted.contains(&target) {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Found single element solution: {}\",\n            target\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(vec![target]), 1);\n    }\n\n    // Precompute prefix sums for pruning (sum of elements 0..=i)\n    let mut prefix_sum = vec![0u64; n + 1];\n    for i in 0..n {\n        prefix_sum[i + 1] = prefix_sum[i].saturating_add(sorted[i]);\n    }\n\n    let mut result_subset: Option<Vec<u64>> = None;\n\n    // Recursive helper that works from the end (largest) towards the start\n    // Returns true if solution found\n    fn recurse(\n        sorted: &[u64],\n        prefix_sum: &[u64],\n        target: u64,\n        end_idx: usize, // exclusive upper bound (elements 0..end_idx available)\n        current_target: u64,\n        subset: &mut Vec<u64>,\n        steps: &mut u64,\n        result: &mut Option<Vec<u64>>,\n        verbose: bool,\n    ) -> bool {\n        *steps += 1;\n\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Step {}: end_idx={}, current_target={}, subset={:?}\",\n            steps,\n            end_idx,\n            current_target,\n            subset\n        );\n\n        // Base case: found exact match\n        if current_target == 0 {\n            *result = Some(subset.clone());\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] Found solution: {:?}\",\n                subset\n            );\n            return true;\n        }\n\n        // No more elements to consider\n        if end_idx == 0 {\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        // Pruning: even taking all remaining elements can't reach target\n        if prefix_sum[end_idx] < current_target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] Pruning: max possible sum {} < target {}\",\n                prefix_sum[end_idx],\n                current_target\n            );\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        // Get the max element (last in the available range)\n        let max_idx = end_idx - 1;\n        let max_val = sorted[max_idx];\n\n        // Case 1: max == current_target → found solution\n        if max_val == current_target {\n            subset.push(max_val);\n            *result = Some(subset.clone());\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] max={} equals target, found solution: {:?}\",\n                max_val,\n                subset\n            );\n            return true;\n        }\n\n        // Case 2: max > current_target → skip this element entirely\n        if max_val > current_target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] max={} > target={}, skipping\",\n                max_val,\n                current_target\n            );\n            return recurse(\n                sorted,\n                prefix_sum,\n                target,\n                max_idx,\n                current_target,\n                subset,\n                steps,\n                result,\n                verbose,\n            );\n        }\n\n        // Case 3: max < current_target → try including, then excluding\n        subset.push(max_val);\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Including max={}, new_target={}\",\n            max_val,\n            current_target - max_val\n        );\n\n        if recurse(\n            sorted,\n            prefix_sum,\n            target,\n            max_idx,\n            current_target - max_val,\n            subset,\n            steps,\n            result,\n            verbose,\n        ) {\n            return true;\n        }\n        subset.pop();\n\n        // Try excluding max\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Excluding max={}, continuing with smaller elements\",\n            max_val\n        );\n\n        recurse(\n            sorted,\n            prefix_sum,\n            target,\n            max_idx,\n            current_target,\n            subset,\n            steps,\n            result,\n            verbose,\n        )\n    }\n\n    recurse(\n        &sorted,\n        &prefix_sum,\n        target,\n        n,\n        target,\n        &mut Vec::new(),\n        &mut steps,\n        &mut result_subset,\n        verbose,\n    );\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Max-First Reduction] Completed with {} steps\",\n        steps\n    );\n    AlgorithmResult::new(result_subset, steps)\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_simple_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n        let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 15, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        let solution = result.solution.unwrap();\n        assert_eq!(solution.iter().sum::<u64>(), 15);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_no_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![2, 4, 6, 8];\n        let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 1, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_none());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_target_zero() {\n        let numbers = vec![1, 2, 3];\n        let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 0, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        assert!(result.solution.unwrap().is_empty());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_single_element() {\n        let numbers = vec![5];\n        let result = assert_eq!(result.solution.unwrap().iter().sum::<u64>(), 10);\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_max_first_behavior() {\n        // When max is part of solution, should find it quickly\n        let numbers = vec![1, 2, 3, 10];\n        let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 13, false); // 10 + 3 = 13\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        let solution =     "originalFile": "//! Max-first reduction algorithm for the subset sum problem.\n//!\n//! This algorithm works by sorting numbers and recursively trying to include\n//! the largest element first. If including the max doesn't lead to a solution,\n//! it's excluded and the search continues with smaller elements.\n//!\n//! The idea is that by committing to the largest elements early, we can\n//! reduce the target sum faster and potentially prune more of the search space.\n\nuse crate::{verbose_log, AlgorithmResult};\n\n/// Max-first reduction subset sum algorithm.\n///\n/// This algorithm:\n/// 1. Sorts numbers in ascending order\n/// 2. Filters out numbers greater than target\n/// 3. Handles edge cases (target = 0, single element solutions, etc.)\n/// 4. Recursively tries to include the largest element:\n///    - If max <= remaining target: include max, recurse with (target - max)\n///    - If no solution found with max, exclude it and try without\n///\n/// The intuition is that larger numbers reduce the target faster,\n/// potentially leading to earlier termination.\n///\n/// # Arguments\n///\n/// * `numbers` - Slice of natural numbers to search through\n/// * `target` - Target sum to find\n/// * `verbose` - Enable verbose logging output\n///\n/// # Returns\n///\n/// `AlgorithmResult` containing the solution (if found) and step count\n///\n/// # Time Complexity\n///\n/// O(2^n) worst case, but with early pruning when large elements\n/// quickly exceed or reach the target.\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// ```\n/// use subset_sum::max_first_reduction;\n///\n/// let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n/// let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 15, false);\n/// assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n/// ```\n#[must_use]\npub fn max_first_reduction(numbers: &[u64], target: u64, verbose: bool) -> AlgorithmResult {\n    let mut steps: u64 = 0;\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Max-First Reduction] Starting with {} numbers, target={}\",\n        numbers.len(),\n        target\n    );\n\n    // Handle target = 0\n    if target == 0 {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Target is 0, returning empty subset\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(Vec::new()), 0);\n    }\n\n    // Filter numbers: keep only those <= target and > 0\n    let mut sorted: Vec<u64> = numbers\n        .iter()\n        .copied()\n        .filter(|&x| x >= 1 && x <= target)\n        .collect();\n\n    if sorted.is_empty() {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] No valid numbers after filtering\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Sort in ascending order (we'll work from the end for max)\n    sorted.sort_unstable();\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Max-First Reduction] Sorted and filtered numbers: {:?}\",\n        sorted\n    );\n\n    let n = sorted.len();\n    let total_sum: u64 = sorted.iter().sum();\n\n    // Early exit: target impossible\n    if target > total_sum {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Target {} > total sum {}, impossible\",\n            target,\n            total_sum\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Check if total sum equals target (take all)\n    if target == total_sum {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Target equals total sum, returning all numbers\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(sorted), 1);\n    }\n\n    // Check for single element solution\n    if sorted.contains(&target) {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Found single element solution: {}\",\n            target\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(vec![target]), 1);\n    }\n\n    // Precompute prefix sums for pruning (sum of elements 0..=i)\n    let mut prefix_sum = vec![0u64; n + 1];\n    for i in 0..n {\n        prefix_sum[i + 1] = prefix_sum[i].saturating_add(sorted[i]);\n    }\n\n    let mut result_subset: Option<Vec<u64>> = None;\n\n    // Recursive helper that works from the end (largest) towards the start\n    // Returns true if solution found\n    fn recurse(\n        sorted: &[u64],\n        prefix_sum: &[u64],\n        end_idx: usize, // exclusive upper bound (elements 0..end_idx available)\n        current_target: u64,\n        subset: &mut Vec<u64>,\n        steps: &mut u64,\n        result: &mut Option<Vec<u64>>,\n        verbose: bool,\n    ) -> bool {\n        *steps += 1;\n\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Step {}: end_idx={}, current_target={}, subset={:?}\",\n            steps,\n            end_idx,\n            current_target,\n            subset\n        );\n\n        // Base case: found exact match\n        if current_target == 0 {\n            *result = Some(subset.clone());\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] Found solution: {:?}\",\n                subset\n            );\n            return true;\n        }\n\n        // No more elements to consider\n        if end_idx == 0 {\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        // Pruning: even taking all remaining elements can't reach target\n        if prefix_sum[end_idx] < current_target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] Pruning: max possible sum {} < target {}\",\n                prefix_sum[end_idx],\n                current_target\n            );\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        // Get the max element (last in the available range)\n        let max_idx = end_idx - 1;\n        let max_val = sorted[max_idx];\n\n        // Case 1: max == current_target → found solution\n        if max_val == current_target {\n            subset.push(max_val);\n            *result = Some(subset.clone());\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] max={} equals target, found solution: {:?}\",\n                max_val,\n                subset\n            );\n            return true;\n        }\n\n        // Case 2: max > current_target → skip this element entirely\n        if max_val > current_target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] max={} > target={}, skipping\",\n                max_val,\n                current_target\n            );\n            return recurse(\n                sorted,\n                prefix_sum,\n                target,\n                max_idx,\n                current_target,\n                subset,\n                steps,\n                result,\n                verbose,\n            );\n        }\n\n        // Case 3: max < current_target → try including, then excluding\n        subset.push(max_val);\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Including max={}, new_target={}\",\n            max_val,\n            current_target - max_val\n        );\n\n        if recurse(\n            sorted,\n            prefix_sum,\n            target,\n            max_idx,\n            current_target - max_val,\n            subset,\n            steps,\n            result,\n            verbose,\n        ) {\n            return true;\n        }\n        subset.pop();\n\n        // Try excluding max\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Excluding max={}, continuing with smaller elements\",\n            max_val\n        );\n\n        recurse(\n            sorted,\n            prefix_sum,\n            target,\n            max_idx,\n            current_target,\n            subset,\n            steps,\n     "originalFile": "//! Max-first reduction algorithm for the subset sum problem.\n//!\n//! This algorithm works by sorting numbers and recursively trying to include\n//! the largest element first. If including the max doesn't lead to a solution,\n//! it's excluded and the search continues with smaller elements.\n//!\n//! The idea is that by committing to the largest elements early, we can\n//! reduce the target sum faster and potentially prune more of the search space.\n\nuse crate::{verbose_log, AlgorithmResult};\n\n/// Max-first reduction subset sum algorithm.\n///\n/// This algorithm:\n/// 1. Sorts numbers in ascending order\n/// 2. Filters out numbers greater than target\n/// 3. Handles edge cases (target = 0, single element solutions, etc.)\n/// 4. Recursively tries to include the largest element:\n///    - If max <= remaining target: include max, recurse with (target - max)\n///    - If no solution found with max, exclude it and try without\n///\n/// The intuition is that larger numbers reduce the target faster,\n/// potentially leading to earlier termination.\n///\n/// # Arguments\n///\n/// * `numbers` - Slice of natural numbers to search through\n/// * `target` - Target sum to find\n/// * `verbose` - Enable verbose logging output\n///\n/// # Returns\n///\n/// `AlgorithmResult` containing the solution (if found) and step count\n///\n/// # Time Complexity\n///\n/// O(2^n) worst case, but with early pruning when large elements\n/// quickly exceed or reach the target.\n///\n/// # Examples\n///\n/// ```\n/// use      \"[Max-First Reduction] Target is 0, returning empty subset\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(Some(Vec::new()), 0);\n    }\n\n    // Filter numbers: keep only those <= target and > 0\n    let mut sorted: Vec<u64> = numbers\n        .iter()\n        .copied()\n        .filter(|&x| x >= 1 && x <= target)\n        .collect();\n\n    if sorted.is_empty() {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] No valid numbers after filtering\"\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Sort in ascending order (we'll work from the end for max)\n    sorted.sort_unstable();\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Max-First Reduction] Sorted and filtered numbers: {:?}\",\n        sorted\n    );\n\n    let n = sorted.len();\n    let total_sum: u64 = sorted.iter().sum();\n\n    // Early exit: target impossible\n    if target > total_sum {\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Target {} > total sum {}, impossible\",\n            target,\n            total_sum\n        );\n        return AlgorithmResult::new(None, 0);\n    }\n\n    // Check if total &[u64],\n        prefix_sum: &[u64],\n        end_idx: usize, // exclusive upper bound (elements 0..end_idx available)\n        current_target: u64,\n        subset: &mut Vec<u64>,\n        steps: &mut u64,\n        result: &mut Option<Vec<u64>>,\n        verbose: bool,\n    ) -> bool {\n        *steps += 1;\n\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Step {}: end_idx={}, current_target={}, subset={:?}\",\n            steps,\n            end_idx,\n            current_target,\n            subset\n        );\n\n        // Base case: found exact match\n        if current_target == 0 {\n            *result = Some(subset.clone());\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] Found solution: {:?}\",\n                subset\n            );\n            return true;\n        }\n\n        // No more elements to consider\n        if end_idx == 0 {\n            return false;\n        }\n\n        // Pruning: even taking all remaining elements can't reach target\n        if prefix_sum[end_idx] < current_target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] Pruning: max possible sum {} < target {}\",\n                prefix_sum[end_idx],\n                current_target\n            );\n            return false;\n        }\n\n if max_val == current_target {\n            subset.push(max_val);\n            *result = Some(subset.clone());\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] max={} equals target, found solution: {:?}\",\n                max_val,\n                subset\n            );\n            return true;\n        }\n\n        // Case 2: max > current_target → skip this element entirely\n        if max_val > current_target {\n            verbose_log!(\n                verbose,\n                \"[Max-First Reduction] max={} > target={}, skipping\",\n                max_val,\n                current_target\n            );\n            return recurse(\n                sorted,\n                prefix_sum,\n                max_idx,\n                current_target,\n                subset,\n                steps,\n                result,\n                verbose,\n            );\n        }\n\n        // Case 3: max < current_target → try including, then excluding\n        subset.push(max_val);\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Including max={}, new_target={}\",\n            max_val,\n            current_target - max_val\n        );\n\n        if recurse(\n            sorted,\n            prefix_sum,\n            max_idx,\n            current_target - max_val,\n            subset,\n            steps,\n            result,\n            verbose,\n        ) {\n            return true;\n        }\n        subset.pop();\n\n        // Try excluding max\n        verbose_log!(\n            verbose,\n            \"[Max-First Reduction] Excluding max={}, continuing with smaller elements\",\n            max_val\n        );\n\n        recurse(\n            sorted,\n            prefix_sum,\n            target,\n            max_idx,\n            current_target,\n            subset,\n            steps,\n            result,\n            verbose,\n        )\n    }\n\n    recurse(\n        &sorted,\n        &prefix_sum,\n        target,\n        n,\n        target,\n        &mut Vec::new(),\n        &mut steps,\n        &mut result_subset,\n        verbose,\n    );\n\n    verbose_log!(\n        verbose,\n        \"[Max-First Reduction] Completed with {} steps\",\n        steps\n    );\n    AlgorithmResult::new(result_subset, steps)\n}\n\n#[cfg(test)]\nmod tests {\n    use super::*;\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_simple_solution() {\n        let numbers = vec![3, 7, 1, 8, 4];\n        let result = }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_target_zero() {\n        let numbers = vec![1, 2, 3];\n        let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 0, false);\n        assert!(result.solution.is_some());\n        assert!(result.solution.unwrap().is_empty());\n    }\n\n    #[test]\n    fn test_single_element() {\n        let numbers = vec![5];\n        let result = max_first_reduction(&numbers, 5, false);\n
